# Codex verification — top-tier gap hunt (#950, concern 7). VERIFY the load-bearing NEW gaps that a Claude Codex Workflow found beyond concerns 1-6. These drive the pre-Q1 build, so confirm or refute precisely by reading the code.

## Gaps to verify (read the files)
1. **S0 — no query decomposition on the live path.** The 5 golden benchmark questions are 40-70-word multi-clause paragraphs. Four (drb_75/76/78/90) ship WITHOUT a hand-authored `amplified` list, so the only content-bearing queries are the full paragraph (and `{paragraph} site:{anchor}`). VERIFY: `scripts/run_honest_sweep_r3.py:~1638` builds `_amplified_effective = list(q.get('amplified', [])) + _reg_queries + _trial_queries`; the no-amplified stubs at `~648-704`; `regulatory_expander.py:~133` prepends the WHOLE paragraph before `site:`; and the PICO decomposer at `src/polaris_graph/clinical_retrieval/query_planner.py:~167` (`plan_queries`) EXISTS but is NOT called from `run_live_retrieval`. Confirm a long multi-clause golden Q is fired essentially as ONE keyword query with no decomposition.
2. **S1 — no fetch-time relevance rerank.** Candidates are truncated by INSERTION ORDER, not relevance. VERIFY: `src/polaris_graph/retrieval/live_retriever.py:~1324` `candidates = candidates[:fetch_cap + _n_seed_injected]`; the prefetch embedding off-topic filter is DISABLED on the sweep (`live_retriever.py:~1173` default `enable_prefetch_filter=False`, and `run_honest_sweep_r3.py:~1664` passes `False`); downstream `evidence_selector.py:~37-40` ranks only by tier + lexical Jaccard over the already-truncated survivors. So early queries saturate the cap and later sub-queries' best hits are truncated pre-fetch.
3. **S1 — analyst-synthesis ships unverified AND un-sanitized.** The Analyst Synthesis layer (~70% of the shipped report) builds raw `<<<evidence:ev_X>>>` blocks with NO `sanitize_evidence_text` call and only `[#ev:...]`/`[N]` syntactic scrubs — no entailment check, no qualitative-negation screen. VERIFY: `src/polaris_graph/generator/analyst_synthesis.py:~285-301` (raw evidence blocks; grep `sanitize` in that file → zero) and `~252-266`/`~184-249` (only the two scrubs); appended to report at `run_honest_sweep_r3.py:~2637-2644`. Confirm the verified multi_section path DOES call `sanitize_evidence_text`/`wrap_evidence_for_prompt` but analyst_synthesis does NOT (Invariant §9.1.7 delimiter-sanitization bypass + the qualitative-negation fabrication class can ship).
4. **S1 — no table/figure structured-results extraction.** Result-table clinical numbers are invisible to provenance. VERIFY: `live_retriever.py:~1098-1156` `_build_provenance_quote` keeps only first 1500 chars + 500-char windows around bare decimals (`-?\d+\.\d+`); `~686-700` `_strip_html` flattens tables; integer-only / no-decimal-% cells aren't captured → strict_verify can only verify numbers surviving as loose decimals in running text.

  111:     Returns:
  112:         A list of `{question} site:{anchor}` strings, one per configured
  113:         anchor (up to `PG_SWEEP_MAX_REGULATORY_ANCHORS` entries). Empty
  114:         list when the template has no `regulatory_anchors` key, an
  115:         empty list, or when the question is empty/whitespace.
  116: 
  117:     This function is pure and deterministic — no network, no state.
  118:     """
  119:     base = (question or "").strip()
  120:     if not base:
  121:         return []
  122:     anchors = _extract_anchors(template)
  123:     if not anchors:
  124:         return []
  125:     cap = _max_anchors()
  126:     if cap > 0 and len(anchors) > cap:
  127:         logger.info(
  128:             "[regulatory_expander] template has %d anchors; capped to %d "
  129:             "via PG_SWEEP_MAX_REGULATORY_ANCHORS",
  130:             len(anchors), cap,
  131:         )

  136:         len(queries), base[:60],
  137:     )
  138:     return queries

 succeeded in 991ms:
  130: 
  131: def _tokens(query: str) -> set[str]:
  132:     return {t.lower() for t in _TOKEN_RE.findall(query)}
  133: 
  134: 
  135: def _jaccard(a: set[str], b: set[str]) -> float:
  136:     if not a and not b:
  137:         return 1.0
  138:     if not a or not b:
  139:         return 0.0
  140:     return len(a & b) / len(a | b)
  141: 
  142: 
  143: def _dedupe(queries: list[str], threshold: float = JACCARD_THRESHOLD) -> list[str]:
  144:     """Drop queries that are >= threshold Jaccard-similar to a kept query.
  145: 
  146:     Order-preserving: earlier queries win, later near-duplicates are
  147:     dropped. This means the cartesian-product base queries (which
  148:     appear before augmented queries) are preferred when a near-dup
  149:     fight breaks out.
  150:     """
  151:     kept: list[str] = []
  152:     kept_tokens: list[set[str]] = []
  153:     for q in queries:
  154:         t = _tokens(q)
  155:         if not t:
  156:             continue
  157:         is_dup = any(
  158:             _jaccard(t, prior) >= threshold for prior in kept_tokens
  159:         )
  160:         if is_dup:
  161:             continue
  162:         kept.append(q)
  163:         kept_tokens.append(t)
  164:     return kept
  165: 
  166: 
  167: def plan_queries(decision: ScopeDecision) -> list[str]:
  168:     """Generate search queries for a ScopeDecision.
  169: 
  170:     Returns up to QUERY_CAP queries, ordered most-specific first.
  171:     Returns [] if the decision has no PICO interpretations to expand
  172:     from (e.g. a refused decision or out-of-scope decision).
  173: 
  174:     Pure function — no I/O, no LLM, no network.
  175:     """
  176:     by_axis = _interpretations_by_axis(decision)
  177:     base = _cartesian_pico(
  178:         by_axis["population"],
  179:         by_axis["intervention"],
  180:         by_axis["outcome"],
  181:     )
  182:     if not base:
  183:         return []
  184: 
  185:     augmented = _augment_with_scope_terms(base, decision.scope_class)
  186:     deduped = _dedupe(augmented)
  187:     return deduped[:QUERY_CAP]

 1060: def is_content_starved(content: str, min_useful_chars: int = 200) -> bool:
 1061:     """R-5 Fix D: detect evidence rows whose fetched content is PDF
 1062:     metadata / formatting fragments / empty text — not useful prose.
 1063: 
 1064:     Returns True if the content should NOT be passed to the generator
 1065:     (because the LLM would admit it has no answer, wasting tokens).
 1066: 
 1067:     Heuristics:
 1068:       - Length of visible text < min_useful_chars
 1069:       - PDF metadata markers dominate
 1070:       - Ratio of alphabetic chars to total chars is low
 1071:     """
 1072:     if not content or len(content.strip()) < min_useful_chars:
 1073:         return True
 1074: 
 1075:     # PDF-metadata dominance check
 1076:     pdf_hits = 0
 1077:     for pat in _PDF_METADATA_PATTERNS:
 1078:         if pat.search(content):
 1079:             pdf_hits += 1
 1080:     if pdf_hits >= 2:
 1081:         return True
 1082: 
 1083:     # Formatting-marker dominance check
 1084:     marker_count = sum(content.count(m) for m in _FORMATTING_NOISE_MARKERS)
 1085:     if marker_count > 20 and marker_count / max(1, len(content) / 100) > 0.5:
 1086:         return True
 1087: 
 1088:     # Alphabetic ratio: if less than 40% of chars are letters, probably
 1089:     # not readable prose (e.g., binary-looking PDF remnants).
 1090:     alpha = sum(1 for ch in content if ch.isalpha())
 1091:     total = len(content)
 1092:     if total > 0 and alpha / total < 0.4:
 1093:         return True
 1094: 
 1095:     return False

 1097: 
 1098: def _build_provenance_quote(
 1099:     content: str,
 1100:     head_chars: int = 1500,
 1101:     window_chars: int = 500,
 1102:     max_total_chars: int = 12000,
 1103:     max_windows: int = 20,
 1104: ) -> str:
 1105:     """Build a direct_quote that contains the head of the document AND
 1106:     500-char windows around every decimal found in the full content.
 1107: 
 1108:     Fixes Fix-3: strict_verify was dropping sentences that cited real
 1109:     numbers living outside the first 1500 chars (e.g., STEP 5 -15.2%
 1110:     in the results section of a Nature paper). Caller stores the result
 1111:     as evidence.direct_quote; Phase 4 _find_span_for_decimal will now
 1112:     find the decimal because a window containing it is in the quote.
 1113: 
 1114:     Returns a concatenation: head || "\\n\\n[...]\\n\\n" || window_1 || ...
 1115:     Deduplicates overlapping windows. Caps total length at max_total_chars
 1116:     to keep prompt budget under control.
 1117:     """
 1118:     if not content:
 1119:         return ""
 1120:     head = content[:head_chars]
 1121:     if len(content) <= head_chars:
 1122:         return head
 1123: 
 1124:     # Find all decimal positions in the full content
 1125:     positions: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
 1126:     for m in _DECIMAL_PATTERN.finditer(content):
 1127:         start = max(0, m.start() - window_chars // 2)
 1128:         end = min(len(content), m.end() + window_chars // 2)
 1129:         positions.append((start, end))
 1130: 
 1131:     # De-overlap: merge adjacent windows that touch each other
 1132:     positions.sort()
 1133:     merged: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
 1134:     for s, e in positions:
 1135:         if merged and s <= merged[-1][1]:
 1136:             merged[-1] = (merged[-1][0], max(merged[-1][1], e))
 1137:         else:
 1138:             merged.append((s, e))
 1139: 
 1140:     # Drop windows already fully inside the head
 1141:     merged = [(s, e) for s, e in merged if e > head_chars]
 1142: 
 1143:     # Cap count
 1144:     merged = merged[:max_windows]
 1145: 
 1146:     chunks = [head]
 1147:     total = len(head)
 1148:     for s, e in merged:
 1149:         chunk = content[s:e]
 1150:         # Stop if we'd exceed the total cap
 1151:         if total + len(chunk) + 6 > max_total_chars:
 1152:             break
 1153:         chunks.append(chunk)
 1154:         total += len(chunk) + 6  # rough separator overhead
 1155: 
 1156:     return "\n\n[...]\n\n".join(chunks)
 1157:

  686: def _strip_html(html: str) -> str:
  687:     """Extract visible text from HTML via basic regex (trafilatura if available)."""
  688:     try:
  689:         import trafilatura  # type: ignore
  690:         extracted = trafilatura.extract(html) or ""
  691:         if extracted:
  692:             return extracted
  693:     except Exception:
  694:         pass
  695:     # Fallback: strip tags + collapse whitespace
  696:     no_tags = re.sub(r"<script[^>]*>.*?</script>", " ", html, flags=re.DOTALL | re.IGNORECASE)
  697:     no_tags = re.sub(r"<style[^>]*>.*?</style>", " ", no_tags, flags=re.DOTALL | re.IGNORECASE)
  698:     no_tags = re.sub(r"<[^>]+>", " ", no_tags)
  699:     no_tags = re.sub(r"\s+", " ", no_tags)
  700:     return no_tags.strip()

  111: # M-42d (2026-04-22): Health Canada quota expansion. V25 baseline had
  112: # 1 HC entry in the bibliography (M-41d reserved 1 slot per present
  113: # jurisdiction). V26 aims for >=2 HC entries covering >=2 distinct
  114: # topics (e.g. monograph + recall/advisory). The expansion is a
  115: # quota-bounded 2nd reservation that ONLY fires after every present
  116: # jurisdiction has its 1st reservation, so FDA/EMA/NICE/MHRA each
  117: # keep their baseline 1 slot regardless of HC's 2nd. Relevance-fill
  118: # still runs afterwards so FDA/EMA/NICE can exceed 1 slot naturally.
  119: #
  120: # Env override `PG_M41D_HC_QUOTA` (default 2). Setting to 1 restores
  121: # exact M-41d behavior (no HC expansion).
  122: _M42D_HC_QUOTA_DEFAULT = 2
  123: _M42D_HC_JURISDICTION_CODE = "HC"

  126: def _m42d_hc_quota() -> int:
  127:     """Return the Health Canada quota (1..N) for the T3 selector floor.
  128: 
  129:     M-42d (2026-04-22): configurable via `PG_M41D_HC_QUOTA` env var.
  130:     Defaults to 2. Values <1 clamp to 1 (legacy M-41d behavior).
  131:     Invalid strings fall back to default.
  132:     """
  133:     raw = os.environ.get("PG_M41D_HC_QUOTA", "")
  134:     if not raw:
  135:         return _M42D_HC_QUOTA_DEFAULT
  136:     try:
  137:         v = int(raw)
  138:     except (ValueError, TypeError):
  139:         return _M42D_HC_QUOTA_DEFAULT
  140:     return max(1, v)

  143: def _row_jurisdiction(row: dict[str, Any]) -> str | None:
  144:     """Return the regulatory jurisdiction code a row belongs to, or
  145:     None if the URL is not from a recognized regulatory host.
  146: 
  147:     M-41d pass-2 (Codex audit medium #3): uses proper host-suffix
  148:     matching instead of substring `in`. Pre-pass-2 `h in url` would
  149:     classify `https://not-fda.gov.example/path` as FDA because the
  150:     literal string `fda.gov` appears in the path. Now we extract the
  151:     actual host component from the URL and require it to either
  152:     equal one of the listed hosts or end with `.{host}` (proper
  153:     subdomain). Plain substring-in-path no longer matches.
  154:     """
  155:     url = (row.get("source_url") or row.get("url") or "").lower()
  156:     if not url:
  157:         return None
  158:     # Extract host: scheme://host/path → host. Be permissive about
  159:     # missing schemes; in that case treat the first path segment as
  160:     # host if it looks like a hostname.
  161:     try:
  162:         from urllib.parse import urlparse
  163:         parsed = urlparse(url if "://" in url else f"http://{url}")
  164:         host = (parsed.hostname or "").lower()
  165:     except (ValueError, AttributeError):
  166:         return None
  167:     if not host:
  168:         return None
  169:     for code, hosts in _M41D_JURISDICTION_HOSTS:
  170:         for h in hosts:
  171:             # Proper suffix match: host == h OR host ends with ".h".
  172:             if host == h or host.endswith("." + h):
  173:                 return code
  174:     return None
  175:

  183: # outscore primary trials on lexical relevance.

  188: # before filling T1 by relevance. Capped at 6 (prevents displacing
  189: # T2 meta-analysis allocation below V25 baseline).

  282: def _row_title_text(row: dict[str, Any]) -> str:
  283:     """M-48 pass-2 (2026-04-22, Codex blocker fix): shared accessor for
  284:     a row's title/title-like text.
  285: 
  286:     Live evidence rows from `run_live_retrieval` populate `statement`
  287:     with `cand.title[:300]` — NOT `title`. Pre-pass-2 accessors only
  288:     read `row["title"]`, silently returning `""` for every live row.
  289:     This broke M-42e primary detection AND M-48 population-scope
  290:     labeling AND the preflight coverage check on real sweep data
  291:     (tests passed only because fixtures used `title`).
  292: 
  293:     Precedence: explicit `title` > `statement` (live-retriever form) >
  294:     `source_title` (alternative schema seen in some retrievers) > "".
  295:     Returns a plain string (never None)."""
  296:     for key in ("title", "statement", "source_title"):
  297:         v = row.get(key)
  298:         if isinstance(v, str) and v:
  299:             return v
  300:     return ""

  303: def _m42c_row_is_mechanism_rich(row: dict[str, Any]) -> bool:
  304:     """True if the row contains mechanism-of-action vocabulary in
  305:     title, statement, or direct_quote. Case-insensitive substring
  306:     match against `_M42C_MECHANISM_TOKENS`."""
  307:     fields = [
  308:         _row_title_text(row),
  309:         str(row.get("statement") or ""),
  310:         str(row.get("direct_quote") or ""),
  311:     ]
  312:     combined = " ".join(fields).lower()
  313:     return any(tok in combined for tok in _M42C_MECHANISM_TOKENS)

  325: def _m42e_detect_primary_for_anchor(
  326:     row: dict[str, Any],
  327:     anchor: str,
  328: ) -> bool:
  329:     """True if `row` appears to be the primary publication for the
  330:     named-trial `anchor` (e.g. 'SURPASS-2', 'SURMOUNT-1').
  331: 
  332:     Detection (M-42e pass-2):
  333:       1. Anchor appears in row title (required).
  334:       2. Row URL/DOI matches a known primary-publication prefix OR
  335:          sits on a primary-publication host.
  336:       3. Row title does NOT match any non-primary-analysis pattern
  337:          (post hoc, subgroup, secondary, exploratory, pooled,
  338:          meta-analysis, substudy, etc.). Even on a primary host, a
  339:          title declaring itself as a post hoc or subgroup analysis
  340:          is NOT the primary publication; usually it's a follow-up
  341:          analysis published in the same or a companion journal.
  342: 
  343:     All three conditions required to prevent tagging analyses as
  344:     primaries.
  345:     """
  346:     if not anchor:
  347:         return False
  348:     # M-48 pass-2 (Codex blocker fix): live retriever populates
  349:     # `statement` not `title`. Use shared accessor.
  350:     title = _row_title_text(row).lower()
  351:     url = (row.get("source_url") or row.get("url") or "").lower()
  352:     anchor_l = anchor.lower()
  353:     # (1) Title must contain the anchor (possibly with colon or
  354:     # parenthesis separator).
  355:     if anchor_l not in title:
  356:         return False
  357:     # (3) Title must NOT contain a non-primary-analysis marker.
  358:     for pat in _M42E_NON_PRIMARY_TITLE_PATTERNS:
  359:         if pat in title:
  360:             return False

  540:         hc_sorted = sorted(hc_rows, key=lambda s: (-s[1], s[0]))
  541:         target = min(hc_quota, len(hc_sorted))
  542:         for item in hc_sorted[:target]:
  543:             m42d_hc_ids.add(id(item))
  544:         m42d_hc_extras = max(0, len(m42d_hc_ids) - 1)
  545:         if m42d_hc_extras > 0:
  546:             notes.append(
  547:                 f"m42d_hc_quota_expand hc_pool={len(hc_rows)} "
  548:                 f"reserved={len(m42d_hc_ids)} "
  549:                 f"extras_added={m42d_hc_extras} quota={hc_quota}"
  550:             )
  551: 
  552:     # --- Deterministic priority ordering ---
  553:     # Priority class: 0 = M-42e primary OR M-51 anchor-primary extra,
  554:     # 1 = M-42c mechanism, 2 = M-42d HC, 3 = rest. Within same class:
  555:     # by tier priority, then -score, then index.
  556:     def _priority_class(item: tuple[int, float, str, dict[str, Any]]) -> int:
  557:         iid = id(item)
  558:         if iid in m42e_ids or iid in m51_extra_ids:
  559:             return 0
  560:         if iid in m42c_ids:
  561:             return 1
  562:         if iid in m42d_hc_ids:
  563:             return 2
  564:         return 3
  565: 
  566:     ordered = sorted(
  567:         scored,
  568:         key=lambda item: (
  569:             _priority_class(item),
  570:             _TIER_PRIORITY.get(item[2], 9),
  571:             -item[1],
  572:             item[0],
  573:         ),
  574:     )
  575:     selected_rows = [item[3] for item in ordered]
  576:     selected_counts = dict(full_counts)
  577: 
  578:     return EvidenceSelection(
  579:         selected_rows=selected_rows,
  580:         full_counts=full_counts,
  581:         selected_counts=selected_counts,
  582:         dropped_count=0,
  583:         selection_strategy="tier_balanced_v1_all_m46_ordered",
  584:         notes=notes,
  585:     )

  588: def select_evidence_for_generation(
  589:     *,
  590:     research_question: str,
  591:     protocol: dict[str, Any] | None,
  592:     classified_sources: list[Any],
  593:     evidence_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
  594:     max_rows: int,
  595:     primary_trial_anchors: list[str] | None = None,
  596: ) -> EvidenceSelection:
  597:     """Pick up to max_rows evidence rows, tier-balanced + relevance-ranked.
  598: 
  599:     Strategy (deterministic, stable):
  600:       1. Join evidence rows to classified sources by URL → tier per row.
  601:       2. Compute full_tier_counts.
  602:       3. Score each row by lexical relevance (question+protocol anchors
  603:          vs statement+direct_quote content words).
  604:       4. Sort within each tier by (-relevance, original_index) for
  605:          deterministic top-N per tier.
  606:       5. Allocate slots proportionally to full_tier_counts but with
  607:          floors for high-value tiers that are present (each T1-T3 tier
  608:          present gets at least min(1, available)).
  609:       6. Fill remaining slots globally by (tier_priority, -relevance,
  610:          original_index).
  611: 
  612:     Args:
  613:         research_question: the user's raw question.
  614:         protocol: scope protocol dict (uses population/intervention/
  615:             comparator/outcome/research_question if present).
  616:         classified_sources: list of objects with .url and .tier (or
  617:             dict-like with those keys). Used for URL→tier join.
  618:         evidence_rows: full evidence row pool.
  619:         max_rows: target selection size.
  620: 
  621:     Returns:
  622:         EvidenceSelection with selected_rows + telemetry.
  623:     """
  624:     if max_rows <= 0 or not evidence_rows:
  625:         return EvidenceSelection(
  626:             selected_rows=[], full_counts={}, selected_counts={},
  627:             dropped_count=0, selection_strategy="tier_balanced_v1",
  628:             notes=["no evidence rows or max_rows <= 0"],
  629:         )
  630: 
  631:     # Build URL → tier map from classified_sources (whatever shape).
  632:     url_to_tier: dict[str, str] = {}
  633:     for src in classified_sources or []:
  634:         url = getattr(src, "url", None) or (
  635:             src.get("url") if isinstance(src, dict) else None
  636:         )
  637:         tier = getattr(src, "tier", None) or (
  638:             src.get("tier") if isinstance(src, dict) else None
  639:         )
  640:         if url and tier:
  641:             url_to_tier[str(url)] = str(tier)
  642: 
  643:     # Compute relevance tokens from research question + protocol anchors.
  644:     question_tokens = _content_tokens(research_question or "")
  645:     protocol_tokens: set[str] = set()
  646:     if protocol:
  647:         for key in ("population", "intervention", "comparator",
  648:                     "outcome", "research_question"):
  649:             v = protocol.get(key)
  650:             if v:
  651:                 protocol_tokens |= _content_tokens(str(v))
  652: 
  653:     # Score every row and tag with tier + original index.
  654:     scored: list[tuple[int, float, str, dict[str, Any]]] = []
  655:     for idx, row in enumerate(evidence_rows):
  656:         tier = _row_tier(row, url_to_tier)
  657:         score = _row_relevance(row, question_tokens, protocol_tokens)
  658:         scored.append((idx, score, tier, row))
  659: 
  660:     # Full tier counts (FROM evidence_rows, the selectable universe).
  661:     full_counts: dict[str, int] = {}
  662:     for _, _, tier, _ in scored:
  663:         full_counts[tier] = full_counts.get(tier, 0) + 1
  664: 
  665:     # M-46 (2026-04-22): when total <= max_rows, still keep everything,
  666:     # BUT compute floor-detection + deterministic priority ordering
  667:     # + telemetry so downstream consumers see the same reservation
  668:     # signals they would see on a truncating run.
  669:     #
  670:     # Pre-M-46 behavior: early-exit branch returned evidence_rows as-is
  671:     # with a single `pool_size<=max_rows` note and no floor telemetry.
  672:     # M-42e primaries, M-42c mechanism rows, and M-42d HC rows were
  673:     # silently not prioritized when pool was small.
  674:     #
  675:     # Post-M-46 behavior: selected list ordered as [M-42e primaries →
  676:     # M-42c mechanism → M-42d HC → rest by (tier priority, -relevance,
  677:     # index)]. All original rows are kept; only ordering changes.
  678:     # Notes include the m42e_primary_floor / m42c_mechanism_floor /
  679:     # m42d_hc_quota_expand entries seen on truncating runs.
  680:     if len(scored) <= max_rows:

  374: 
  375: def _row_relevance(
  376:     row: dict[str, Any],
  377:     question_tokens: set[str],
  378:     protocol_tokens: set[str],
  379: ) -> float:
  380:     """Deterministic lexical relevance score in [0, 1].
  381: 
  382:     Overlap between the union of question+protocol tokens and the
  383:     evidence's statement+direct_quote content tokens. Jaccard-ish but
  384:     normalized by the question side so longer evidence doesn't dominate.
  385:     """
  386:     text = " ".join(str(row.get(k, "") or "") for k in ("statement", "direct_quote"))
  387:     ev_toks = _content_tokens(text)
  388:     anchors = question_tokens | protocol_tokens
  389:     if not anchors:
  390:         return 0.0
  391:     overlap = ev_toks & anchors
  392:     return len(overlap) / max(1, len(anchors))

  116: # I-bug-110: process-lifetime telemetry for synthesis [N] scrub.
  117: # When the synthesis LLM hallucinates [N] markers beyond the
  118: # bibliography size, _scrub_invalid_n_markers strips them at runtime.
  119: # An operator monitoring synthesis quality wants two signals:
  120: #   - synthesis_n_scrub_count: total markers scrubbed across this
  121: #     process's lifetime (cumulative).
  122: #   - synthesis_n_scrub_runs: number of synthesis calls that needed
  123: #     ANY scrub (i.e., at least one invalid marker present).
  124: # These mirror the entailment-judge telemetry pattern at
  125: # polaris_graph.llm.entailment_judge._JUDGE_TELEMETRY.
  126: _SYNTHESIS_TELEMETRY: dict[str, int] = {
  127:     "synthesis_n_scrub_count": 0,
  128:     "synthesis_n_scrub_runs": 0,
  129: }
  130: 
  131: 
  132: # I-bug-111: WARN-level alert threshold per single scrub call. When
  133: # synthesis hallucinates >5 [N] markers in ONE call, the bibliography
  134: # rendering / synthesis prompt is likely degenerating (typical clean
  135: # runs scrub 0; a healthy run with one stray hallucination scrubs 1-2).
  136: # Operators see a distinct "synthesis_n_scrub_alert" log + the manifest
  137: # bool flag below.
  138: SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_THRESHOLD = 5
  139: 
  140: _SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_FIRED = False
  141: 
  142: 
  143: def synthesis_scrub_alert_state() -> bool:
  144:     """Return True if any scrub call in this process exceeded the
  145:     alert threshold (`SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_THRESHOLD`).
  146: 
  147:     Operator-facing: aggregators (sweep manifest writers) read this
  148:     once at end-of-run and surface the bool as
  149:     `manifest.synthesis_n_scrub_alert`. The flag is sticky across
  150:     calls (true if any single call tripped it) — a transient spike
  151:     in any one call is still worth surfacing.
  152:     """
  153:     return _SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_FIRED
  154: 
  155: 
  156: def reset_synthesis_scrub_alert() -> None:
  157:     """Reset the sticky alert flag in-place. Tests + sweep
  158:     orchestrators call this at start-of-run.
  159:     """
  160:     global _SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_FIRED
  161:     _SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_FIRED = False
  162: 
  163: 
  164: def get_synthesis_telemetry() -> dict[str, int]:
  165:     """Snapshot of process-lifetime synthesis-scrub counters.
  166: 
  167:     Operator-facing: the existence of any scrub on a production run
  168:     is a signal the synthesis prompt or bibliography rendering may
  169:     be drifting. Aggregated trends should be tracked.
  170:     """
  171:     return dict(_SYNTHESIS_TELEMETRY)
  172: 
  173: 
  174: def reset_synthesis_telemetry() -> None:
  175:     """Zero all synthesis-telemetry counters in-place.
  176: 
  177:     Public so callers (sweep orchestrators, tests) can deliberately
  178:     bound the counter window to a single run.
  179:     """
  180:     for key in _SYNTHESIS_TELEMETRY:
  181:         _SYNTHESIS_TELEMETRY[key] = 0
  182: 
  183: 
  184: def _scrub_invalid_n_markers(text: str, biblio_size: int) -> tuple[str, int]:
  185:     """Remove [N] bibliography markers where N is invalid.
  186: 
  187:     Invalid means:
  188:       - N > biblio_size (out-of-range hallucination)
  189:       - N < 1 (zero, negative — bibliography indices start at 1)
  190:       - whitespace-padded forms like [ 5 ] (parser-fragile)
  191: 
  192:     I-bug-108 P0 fix: the synthesis LLM occasionally hallucinates [N]
  193:     indices beyond the bibliography. The downstream evaluator rule
  194:     PT12 (rule_pt12_invalid_citation_marker) aborts the report when
  195:     max_marker > evidence_pool size. Scrub them runtime so production
  196:     runs don't abort. Returns (cleaned_text, num_scrubbed).
  197: 
  198:     Iter-2 P0 hardening per Codex review: also catch [-N], [ N ],
  199:     [01], etc. — anything that looks like a citation marker but isn't
  200:     a valid 1..biblio_size index.
  201:     """
  202:     scrubbed = 0
  203: 
  204:     def _replace(match: re.Match) -> str:
  205:         nonlocal scrubbed
  206:         try:
  207:             n = int(match.group(1))
  208:         except (ValueError, TypeError):
  209:             scrubbed += 1
  210:             return ""
  211:         if n < 1 or n > biblio_size:
  212:             scrubbed += 1
  213:             return ""  # drop the invalid marker entirely
  214:         # Also drop if the original raw form had padding/leading zero
  215:         # (bibliography emits "[1]" not "[ 1 ]" or "[01]")
  216:         raw = match.group(0)
  217:         canonical = f"[{n}]"
  218:         if raw != canonical:
  219:             scrubbed += 1
  220:             return ""
  221:         return raw
  222: 
  223:     cleaned = _MALFORMED_MARKER_RE.sub(_replace, text)
  224:     if scrubbed > 0:
  225:         logger.warning(
  226:             "[analyst_synthesis] scrubbed %d invalid [N] marker(s) "
  227:             "(out-of-range OR malformed; biblio_size=%d) — "
  228:             "synthesis LLM hallucinated indices",
  229:             scrubbed, biblio_size,
  230:         )
  231:         # I-bug-110: increment process-lifetime telemetry counters.
  232:         # synthesis_n_scrub_count is total marker count; synthesis_n_scrub_runs
  233:         # is the number of synthesis calls that needed any scrub.
  234:         _SYNTHESIS_TELEMETRY["synthesis_n_scrub_count"] += scrubbed
  235:         _SYNTHESIS_TELEMETRY["synthesis_n_scrub_runs"] += 1
  236:         # I-bug-111: trip the sticky alert flag on any high-scrub call.
  237:         # Threshold = 5 markers in ONE call — typical healthy synthesis
  238:         # scrubs 0; the I-bug-108 incident scrubbed 6 in one call,
  239:         # validating this threshold empirically.
  240:         if scrubbed > SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_THRESHOLD:
  241:             global _SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_FIRED
  242:             _SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_FIRED = True
  243:             logger.warning(
  244:                 "[analyst_synthesis] synthesis_n_scrub_alert: %d markers "
  245:                 "scrubbed in single call (threshold=%d). Synthesis "
  246:                 "prompt or bibliography rendering may be degenerating.",
  247:                 scrubbed, SYNTHESIS_SCRUB_ALERT_THRESHOLD,
  248:             )
  249:     return cleaned, scrubbed
  250: 
  251: 
  252: def _scrub_ev_tokens(text: str) -> str:
  253:     """Remove any [#ev:...] tokens from synthesis output.
  254: 
  255:     Codex iter-1 P0: must be a runtime guardrail, not just a test.
  256:     Synthesis prose MUST NOT carry [#ev:...] tokens. If the LLM emits
  257:     them anyway, scrub them and log a warning.
  258:     """
  259:     cleaned, n = _EV_TOKEN_RE.subn("", text)
  260:     if n > 0:
  261:         logger.warning(
  262:             "[analyst_synthesis] scrubbed %d [#ev:...] token(s) from "
  263:             "synthesis output — synthesis MUST cite by [N] only",
  264:             n,
  265:         )
  266:     return cleaned
  267: 
  268: 
  269: def _format_bibliography_for_prompt(bibliography: list[dict[str, Any]]) -> str:
  270:     """Render the global bibliography as numbered [N] entries for the prompt.
  271: 
  272:     Mirrors the bibliography format the Verified Findings section already
  273:     uses, so the synthesis cites the same [N] indices the audit core does.
  274:     """
  275:     lines = []
  276:     for i, entry in enumerate(bibliography, start=1):
  277:         title = entry.get("title") or "Untitled"
  278:         url = entry.get("url") or ""
  279:         tier = entry.get("tier") or ""
  280:         tier_str = f" (tier {tier})" if tier else ""
  281:         lines.append(f"[{i}] {title} — {url}{tier_str}")
  282:     return "\n".join(lines)
  283: 
  284: 
  285: def _format_evidence_pool_for_prompt(
  286:     evidence_rows: list[dict[str, Any]],
  287:     max_rows: int = 30,
  288: ) -> str:
  289:     """Render the evidence pool as <<<evidence:ev_X>>> blocks the LLM
  290:     can read for context. Capped at max_rows to bound the prompt size.
  291:     """
  292:     blocks = []
  293:     for row in evidence_rows[:max_rows]:
  294:         ev_id = row.get("evidence_id") or row.get("id") or "ev_?"
  295:         quote = (
  296:             row.get("direct_quote")
  297:             or row.get("statement")
  298:             or ""
  299:         )[:1200]
  300:         blocks.append(f"<<<evidence:{ev_id}>>>\n{quote}\n<<<end>>>")
  301:     return "\n\n".join(blocks)

  241: def sanitize_evidence_text(text: str) -> tuple[str, int]:
  242:     """Redact prompt-injection patterns AND delimiter literals from evidence.
  243: 
  244:     B-5 fix (Codex round 1 blocker): in addition to the classical
  245:     prompt-injection directives, this also redacts the exact delimiter
  246:     strings used by the generator wrapper (<<<evidence:...>>>,
  247:     <<<end_evidence>>>, <<<pipeline_telemetry>>>, <<<end_telemetry>>>).
  248:     Without this, evidence content could forge a closing delimiter and
  249:     a new opening delimiter, breaking out of the DATA block into a
  250:     spoofed block the generator would treat as authentic.
  251: 
  252:     Codex round 3 architectural fix: the prior version globally
  253:     rewrote the whole string (NFKC + invisible-strip + confusable-map),
  254:     which silently mutated legitimate Cyrillic/Greek evidence content.
  255:     The new approach builds a normalized VIEW, runs delimiter regexes
  256:     on the view, and redacts the corresponding ranges in the ORIGINAL
  257:     text. Non-delimiter content is byte-preserved. Delimiter lookalikes
  258:     (NFKC variants, invisible-char embeds, cross-script homoglyphs)
  259:     are still caught.
  260: 
  261:     Returns (sanitized_text, num_redactions).
  262:     """
  263:     if not text:
  264:         return "", 0
  265:     out = text
  266:     redactions = 0
  267:     # Pass 1: classical injection directives on the RAW text. These
  268:     # patterns target ASCII directives that don't need normalization.
  269:     for pat in _INJECTION_PATTERNS:
  270:         new, n = pat.subn(_REDACTION, out)
  271:         if n > 0:
  272:             redactions += n
  273:             out = new
  274:     # Pass 2: delimiter-literal redaction via normalized view with
  275:     # index projection back to the (post-pass-1) original.
  276:     normalized, orig_idx = _build_normalized_view(out)
  277:     # Collect ranges to redact, expressed as (original_start, original_end).
  278:     ranges: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
  279:     for pat in _DELIMITER_LITERAL_PATTERNS:
  280:         for m in pat.finditer(normalized):
  281:             ns, ne = m.start(), m.end()
  282:             if ns >= len(orig_idx) or ne == 0:
  283:                 continue
  284:             orig_start = orig_idx[ns]
  285:             orig_end = (
  286:                 orig_idx[ne - 1] + 1 if ne - 1 < len(orig_idx)
  287:                 else len(out)
  288:             )
  289:             ranges.append((orig_start, orig_end))
  290:     if ranges:
  291:         # Merge overlapping ranges and apply in reverse (preserves indices)
  292:         ranges.sort()
  293:         merged: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
  294:         for s, e in ranges:
  295:             if merged and s <= merged[-1][1]:
  296:                 merged[-1] = (merged[-1][0], max(merged[-1][1], e))
  297:             else:
  298:                 merged.append((s, e))
  299:         for s, e in reversed(merged):
  300:             out = out[:s] + _DELIMITER_REDACTION + out[e:]
  301:             redactions += 1
  302:     return out, redactions
  303:

  325:             total_red, evidence_id,

  337: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  338: # Provenance token parsing
  339: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  340: 
  341: # Pattern: [#ev:<evidence_id>:<start>-<end>]
  342: # Example: [#ev:ev_step1:12-45]

src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:712:12. **Primary-study framing (M-32, for claim-frame rigor)**: When you name a primary study, trial, cohort, experiment, or any individually identifiable empirical data source, and the cited evidence rows contain the structured metadata, provide the study's FULL FRAME in the FIRST sentence that introduces it: (a) sample size or cohort size (e.g. N=1879), (b) baseline value of the outcome being discussed (e.g. mean baseline [PRIMARY_METRIC]=[VALUE], baseline [SECONDARY_METRIC]=[VALUE]), (c) comparator / control / background condition (e.g. versus [COMPARATOR], versus placebo on [BACKGROUND], versus standard [REFERENCE_CONDITION]), and (d) the primary endpoint + timepoint (e.g. [ENDPOINT] change at [TIMEPOINT], [N-YEAR] [OUTCOME_TYPE], cycle-life to [THRESHOLD] retention). If the evidence row carries this structured metadata, you MUST emit it in that first sentence — do not compress N/baseline/endpoint into a single percent-reduction when the evidence carries the full frame. This is what distinguishes a research-grade deep synthesis from a news-style summary. Example template: "In [STUDY NAME], [STUDY_DESIGN_SUMMARY] randomized N=[SAMPLE_SIZE] participants with baseline [OUTCOME]=[BASELINE_VALUE] to [INTERVENTION] versus [COMPARATOR]; [PRIMARY_ENDPOINT] at [TIMEPOINT] was [RESULT] [ev_X]." Subsequent sentences about the same study may reference it by short name without re-framing. Generalizable beyond clinical: a materials paper gets composition + baseline performance + test condition + measured outcome; a cohort study gets population + baseline metric + intervention + outcome; a financial filing gets period + baseline metric + policy/benchmark + reported outcome.
src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:715:13. **Policy-scope disambiguation (M-NEW-1, GH#422)**: When a paragraph names a specific program (Bill C-64, ACA, MACRA, EU AI Act, Article 34.7 CUSMA review, a particular budget line, etc.) and the evidence pool also contains projections / cost estimates / impact analyses for a RELATED-BUT-BROADER scope (universal single-payer projection vs phase-1 narrow program; comprehensive coverage estimate vs narrow amendment; multi-jurisdiction equivalent of a single-state rule), do NOT silently fold the broader projection into the narrow-program paragraph. When citing numbers from the broader scope, EXPLICITLY label the scope-attribution INLINE in the SAME sentence as the citation. Required pattern: write "PBO 2023 universal single-payer projection estimates the additional cost at $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" — NOT "the incremental cost is $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_X]" inside a paragraph that opens with Bill C-64 phase-1 (which covers only contraception and diabetes medications). The decimal and the citation are correct; the missing scope label is what makes the conflation. Same evidence-ID, additional 4-8 word scope phrase before the citation. This rule fires regardless of which section the named-program paragraph appears in (Regulatory, Comparative, Economic, etc.). Failure mode this rule prevents: a reader concludes a narrow program will cost the broader program's projected figure. Concrete examples (placeholders only): GOOD: "Bill C-64 covers a defined set of contraception and diabetes medications [ev_A]. The PBO's 2023 cost estimate of a universal single-payer drug plan modeled on an expanded Quebec formulary projects incremental public-sector cost of $11.2B in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — distinct scopes named, decimals attributed to broader scope. BAD: "Under Bill C-64, the incremental cost to the public sector is estimated at $11.2 billion in 2024-25 [ev_B]." — cites the PBO universal-plan source as if it were a Bill C-64 phase-1 projection.

    1: """
    2: Domain-specific retrieval backends — HONEST-REBUILD R-6 Gap-2.
    3: 
    4: Each domain (clinical / policy / tech / due_diligence) has unique
    5: authoritative sources that generic Serper+S2 misses:
    6: 
    7:   clinical:     PubMed / ClinicalTrials.gov / Cochrane — already well-
    8:                 covered by S2 academic search, no new backend needed.
    9: 
   10:   policy:       Federal Register, agency guidance pages. Implemented
   11:                 via targeted Serper queries with site: operators so the
   12:                 same Serper budget gets policy-authoritative hits.
   13: 
   14:   tech:         arXiv API (direct, not via S2) for preprints and
   15:                 conference papers. GitHub README fetching for
   16:                 open-source project documentation.
   17: 
   18:   due_diligence:  SEC EDGAR full-text search for 10-K / 10-Q / 8-K
   19:                 filings — primary documents of record for public
   20:                 companies. No API key needed.
   21: 
   22: DESIGN:
   23:   - Each backend returns SearchCandidate objects (same shape as the
   24:     generic retriever), so the caller merges them transparently.
   25:   - Each backend has a hard cap on the number of hits it contributes
   26:     (PG_DOMAIN_MAX_HITS env var, default 10).
   27:   - Backends fail open: if arXiv / SEC / Federal Register API is down
   28:     or throws, return empty list and log; don't break retrieval.
   29: """
   30: from __future__ import annotations
   31: 
   32: import logging
   33: import os
   34: import re
   35: from dataclasses import dataclass
   36: from typing import Any
   37: from urllib.parse import quote_plus

   51: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   52: # Shared httpx helper
   53: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   54: 
   55: 
   56: def _http_get_json(url: str, params: dict | None = None) -> dict | None:
   57:     try:
   58:         with httpx.Client(
   59:             timeout=HTTP_TIMEOUT,
   60:             follow_redirects=True,
   61:             headers={"User-Agent": "POLARIS-honest-rebuild/1.0"},
   62:         ) as c:
   63:             r = c.get(url, params=params)
   64:         if r.status_code != 200:
   65:             return None
   66:         try:
   67:             return r.json()
   68:         except Exception:
   69:             return None
   70:     except Exception as exc:
   71:         logger.debug("http_get_json %r failed: %s", url, exc)
   72:         return None
   73: 
   74: 
   75: def _http_get_text(url: str, params: dict | None = None) -> str | None:
   76:     try:
   77:         with httpx.Client(
   78:             timeout=HTTP_TIMEOUT,
   79:             follow_redirects=True,
   80:             headers={"User-Agent": "POLARIS-honest-rebuild/1.0"},
   81:         ) as c:
   82:             r = c.get(url, params=params)
   83:         if r.status_code != 200:
   84:             return None
   85:         return r.text
   86:     except Exception as exc:
   87:         logger.debug("http_get_text %r failed: %s", url, exc)
   88:         return None
   89: 
   90: 
   91: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   92: # TECH: arXiv
   93: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   94: 
   95: _ARXIV_API = "http://export.arxiv.org/api/query"
   96: 
   97: 
   98: def _parse_arxiv_feed(xml: str, limit: int) -> list[SearchCandidate]:
   99:     if not xml:
  100:         return []
  101:     # Minimal Atom XML parsing without pulling a dependency. arXiv
  102:     # returns predictable structure.
  103:     candidates: list[SearchCandidate] = []
  104:     # Entries are <entry>...</entry>
  105:     entries = re.findall(r"<entry>(.*?)</entry>", xml, flags=re.DOTALL)
  106:     for e in entries[:limit]:
  107:         title_m = re.search(r"<title>(.*?)</title>", e, flags=re.DOTALL)
  108:         summary_m = re.search(r"<summary>(.*?)</summary>", e, flags=re.DOTALL)
  109:         id_m = re.search(r"<id>(.*?)</id>", e, flags=re.DOTALL)
  110:         if not id_m:
  111:             continue
  112:         arxiv_url = id_m.group(1).strip()
  113:         # Prefer the abs URL (html) over PDF
  114:         if "/abs/" not in arxiv_url:
  115:             arxiv_url = arxiv_url.replace("http://", "https://")
  116:         title = (title_m.group(1).strip() if title_m else "")
  117:         # Collapse whitespace
  118:         title = re.sub(r"\s+", " ", title)
  119:         summary = (summary_m.group(1).strip() if summary_m else "")
  120:         summary = re.sub(r"\s+", " ", summary)[:400]
  121:         candidates.append(SearchCandidate(
  122:             url=arxiv_url, title=title, snippet=summary, source="arxiv",
  123:         ))
  124:     return candidates
  125: 
  126: 
  127: def arxiv_search(query: str, limit: int = PG_DOMAIN_MAX_HITS) -> list[SearchCandidate]:
  128:     """Query arXiv via the Atom API. Fail-open."""
  129:     params = {
  130:         "search_query": f"all:{query}",
  131:         "start": 0,
  132:         "max_results": max(1, min(limit, 30)),
  133:         "sortBy": "relevance",
  134:         "sortOrder": "descending",
  135:     }
  136:     xml = _http_get_text(_ARXIV_API, params=params)
  137:     if not xml:
  138:         return []
  139:     try:
  140:         return _parse_arxiv_feed(xml, limit)
  141:     except Exception as exc:
  142:         logger.warning("[domain_backends] arxiv parse failed: %s", exc)
  143:         return []

  164: def policy_targeted_serper(
  165:     query: str, limit: int = PG_DOMAIN_MAX_HITS,
  166: ) -> list[SearchCandidate]:
  167:     """Issue a Serper query with a policy-site OR clause.
  168: 
  169:     The policy domain's authoritative sources are regulatory agency
  170:     pages. Rather than spin up a new API, we use Serper with a
  171:     `(site:federalregister.gov OR site:fda.gov OR ...)` bundle so the
  172:     same API budget returns policy-biased results.
  173:     """
  174:     api_key = os.getenv("SERPER_API_KEY", "").strip()
  175:     if not api_key:
  176:         return []
  177:     # I-safety-002b (#925) PR-2: record serper attempt for the Path-B gate (best-effort).
  178:     try:
  179:         from src.polaris_graph.benchmark import pathB_capture as _pathb
  180:         _pathb.record_retrieval_attempt("serper")
  181:     except Exception:
  182:         pass
  183:     site_clause = " OR ".join(_POLICY_SITE_FILTERS)
  184:     q = f"{query} ({site_clause})"
  185:     try:
  186:         with httpx.Client(timeout=HTTP_TIMEOUT) as c:
  187:             r = c.post(
  188:                 "https://google.serper.dev/search",
  189:                 headers={"X-API-KEY": api_key, "Content-Type": "application/json"},
  190:                 json={"q": q, "num": max(1, min(limit, 20))},
  191:             )
  192:         if r.status_code != 200:
  193:             return []
  194:         data = r.json()
  195:     except Exception as exc:
  196:         logger.debug("[domain_backends] policy serper failed: %s", exc)
  197:         return []
  198:     out: list[SearchCandidate] = []
  199:     for item in (data.get("organic") or [])[:limit]:
  200:         url = item.get("link", "") or ""
  201:         if not url:
  202:             continue
  203:         out.append(SearchCandidate(
  204:             url=url,
  205:             title=item.get("title", "") or "",
  206:             snippet=item.get("snippet", "") or "",
  207:             source="serper_policy",
  208:         ))
  209:     return out

  212: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  213: # DUE DILIGENCE: SEC EDGAR full-text search
  214: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
  215: 
  216: _SEC_SEARCH_URL = "https://efts.sec.gov/LATEST/search-index"
  217: 
  218: 
  219: def sec_edgar_search(
  220:     query: str, limit: int = PG_DOMAIN_MAX_HITS,
  221: ) -> list[SearchCandidate]:
  222:     """Full-text search SEC EDGAR for 10-K / 10-Q / 8-K / DEF 14A.
  223: 
  224:     No API key required. Fail-open.
  225:     """
  226:     params = {
  227:         "q": query,
  228:         "dateRange": "custom",
  229:         "startdt": "2019-01-01",
  230:         "forms": "10-K,10-Q,8-K,DEF 14A,S-1",
  231:     }
  232:     data = _http_get_json(_SEC_SEARCH_URL, params=params)
  233:     if not data:
  234:         return []
  235:     hits = data.get("hits", {}).get("hits", []) or []

  743: def refetch_for_extraction(url: str, max_chars: int = 2000) -> str:
  744:     """M-42b (2026-04-22): re-fetch source content for deterministic
  745:     trial-table / timeline extraction when the evidence row's
  746:     existing `direct_quote` is thin (<100 chars) or the row was
  747:     never successfully fetched.
  748: 
  749:     Returns a 2000-char extract (head + decimal-windows) via
  750:     _fetch_content + _build_provenance_quote, or empty string when
  751:     the URL cannot be fetched or returns thin content.
  752: 
  753:     Caller is expected to cache the result on the evidence row for
  754:     the remainder of the run so repeat table generation within the
  755:     same sweep does not re-hit the network.
  756: 
  757:     Generic wrapper — not trial/drug/domain-specific. Used by the
  758:     M-42b trial-table builder and the Trial Program Timeline builder.
  759: 
  760:     M-45 (2026-04-22): see `refetch_for_extraction_with_diagnostics`
  761:     for a variant that returns structured per-URL diagnostics
  762:     (backend, char count, body type, eligibility, failure mode) for
  763:     the V28 preflight and downstream audits. This function is a thin
  764:     wrapper around that variant.
  765:     """
  766:     quote, _diag = refetch_for_extraction_with_diagnostics(url, max_chars)

  770: # M-45 pass-2 (Codex audit HIGH): per-URL method + failure-reason
  771: # telemetry. Module-level dict populated by `_fetch_content` just
  772: # before it returns, then read by `refetch_for_extraction_with_
  773: # diagnostics`. Keyed by url; overwritten on each call so memory
  774: # stays bounded. Not thread-safe for concurrent refetches of the
  775: # same URL, but the current sweep path is sequential per URL.
  776: _M45_LAST_FETCH_TELEMETRY: dict[str, dict[str, Any]] = {}
  777: 
  778: 
  779: def _m45_record_fetch_telemetry(
  780:     url: str, method: str, failure_reason: str = "",
  781: ) -> None:
  782:     """M-45 pass-2: record the final AccessBypass method + failure
  783:     reason for a fetch call. Overwrites any prior entry for the same
  784:     URL so repeat refetches in one run show the latest attempt."""
  785:     _M45_LAST_FETCH_TELEMETRY[url] = {
  786:         "method": method or "unknown",
  787:         "failure_reason": failure_reason,
  788:     }
  789: 
  790: 
  791: def _m45_pop_fetch_telemetry(url: str) -> dict[str, Any]:
  792:     """M-45 pass-2: read + remove the telemetry for a URL so it's
  793:     not reused by a later unrelated call. Returns empty dict if no
  794:     entry was recorded."""
  795:     return _M45_LAST_FETCH_TELEMETRY.pop(url, {})

  798: def refetch_for_extraction_with_diagnostics(
  799:     url: str, max_chars: int = 2000,
  800: ) -> tuple[str, dict[str, Any]]:
  801:     """M-45 (2026-04-22): refetch with structured per-URL diagnostics.
  802: 
  803:     Codex V28 plan pass-2 APPROVED this diagnostic-first approach.
  804:     V27 still produced thin quotes for paywalled PDFs despite the
  805:     AccessBypass cascade existing. This variant records WHY each
  806:     refetch landed or failed so audits can branch the fix
  807:     (explicit-wire Jina/Firecrawl, better extraction window, or
  808:     strict skip) based on real data instead of assumption.
  809: 
  810:     Returns (quote, diagnostics) where:
  811:       - quote: same as `refetch_for_extraction` — non-empty iff the
  812:         refetched content is ≥100 chars and the provenance quote
  813:         was built; empty string otherwise. Strict ≥100 char contract
  814:         preserved (no statement fallback, no prose fallback).
  815:       - diagnostics: dict with these keys:
  816:           url: the input URL (truncated to 200 chars for JSON safety)
  817:           attempted: bool — did we try the fetch at all
  818:           method: str — AccessBypass method that produced content
  819:             ('crawl4ai', 'jina', 'firecrawl', 'httpx', 'archive_org',
  820:             'scihub', or 'none')
  821:           raw_char_count: int — bytes returned by _fetch_content
  822:             before provenance-quote extraction
  823:           body_type: str — 'abstract' / 'full_text' / 'paywall_shell'
  824:             / 'html_meta' per `_detect_article_type_from_body`
  825:           eligible: bool — True iff quote was emitted (≥100 chars)

  379: 
  380: # Safety endpoint vocab for table-row headers. Mirrors the safety subset
  381: # of _ENDPOINT_VOCAB so any row labeled with a known safety endpoint
  382: # becomes a per-cell extraction candidate.
  383: _SAFETY_TABLE_HEADER_RE = re.compile(
  384:     r"(?:"
  385:     r"^|^\W+|"  # row prefix tolerant (markdown bullets, leading symbols)
  386:     r"\b"
  387:     r")"
  388:     r"(?P<endpoint>"
  389:     r"nausea|vomiting|diarrh(?:o)?ea|constipation|abdominal\s+pain|"
  390:     r"dyspepsia|decreased\s+appetite|"
  391:     r"hypoglycem(?:ia|ic)|"
  392:     r"pancreatitis|gallbladder(?:\s+disease)?|cholelithiasis|cholecystitis|"
  393:     r"retinopathy|"
  394:     r"injection[-\s]?site\s+reactions?|"
  395:     r"(?:all\s+)?(?:treatment[-\s]?related\s+|treatment[-\s]?emergent\s+)?"
  396:     r"adverse\s+events?(?:\s+leading\s+to\s+(?:treatment\s+)?discontinuation"
  397:     r"(?:\s+of\s+\w+(?:\s+(?:or|and)\s+\w+)?)?)?|"
  398:     r"TEAE|"
  399:     r"serious\s+adverse\s+events?|SAEs?|"
  400:     r"discontinuation|treatment\s+withdrawal|"
  401:     r"patients\s+with\s+(?:≥|>=|≧)\s*1\s+(?:serious\s+)?adverse\s+events?|"
  402:     r"patients\s+with\s+at\s+least\s+1\s+(?:serious\s+)?adverse\s+events?|"
  403:     r"(?:all\s+)?gastrointestinal\s+(?:adverse\s+)?events?|"
  404:     r"(?:all\s+)?GI\s+(?:adverse\s+)?events?|"
  405:     r"thyroid\s+(?:carcinoma|cancer|c[-\s]?cell)|MTC|"
  406:     r"C[-\s]?cell\s+(?:hyperplasia|cancer)|"
  407:     r"GI\s+bleeding|gastrointestinal\s+bleeding|major\s+bleeding|"
  408:     r"intracranial\s+hemorrhage|ICH|"
  409:     # Codex Step 3k diff iter-1 P2 #2: expanded vocab for fresh tables
  410:     r"death|all[-\s]?cause\s+mortality|"
  411:     r"fatigue|asthenia|headache|dizziness|"
  412:     r"hypersensitivity|allergic\s+reactions?|anaphylaxis|"
  413:     r"acute\s+kidney\s+injury|AKI|renal\s+(?:impairment|failure)|"
  414:     r"neoplasm|cancer|malignancy|"
  415:     r"calcitonin|"
  416:     r"hyperglycem(?:ia|ic)|"
  417:     r"infection|"
  418:     r"urinary\s+tract\s+infection|UTI|"
  419:     r"upper\s+respiratory\s+tract\s+infection|URTI|"
  420:     r"nasopharyngitis"
  421:     r")",
  422:     re.IGNORECASE,
  423: )
  424: 
  425: # Cell percentage extraction:
  426: #   - Number followed by % → that number
  427: #   - Number inside (...) → that number (canonical "n (pct)" form)
  428: # Bare numbers are SKIPPED per Codex Step 3k P2 (column-header parsing
  429: # required to know if bare numbers are percentages vs counts).
  430: _CELL_PCT_TRAILING_RE = re.compile(r"(?P<val>\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*%")
  431: _CELL_PCT_PAREN_RE = re.compile(r"\(\s*(?P<val>\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*\)")
  432: 
  433: 
  434: def _canonicalize_safety_endpoint(raw: str) -> str:
  435:     """Map a raw safety table header to the canonical endpoint name
  436:     used elsewhere in the catalog (matching _ENDPOINT_VOCAB entries).
  437:     """
  438:     r = raw.strip().lower()
  439:     if "serious adverse" in r or re.match(r"^saes?$", r) or "≥1 serious adverse" in r:
  440:         return "serious adverse events"
  441:     if "leading to" in r and ("discontinuation" in r or "treatment withdrawal" in r):
  442:         return "discontinuation"
  443:     if "≥1 adverse event" in r or r in ("teae", "adverse event", "adverse events"):
  444:         return "adverse events"
  445:     if "gastrointestinal" in r or r in ("gi events", "gi adverse events"):
  446:         return "GI events"
  447:     if "injection" in r and "site" in r:
  448:         return "injection-site reaction"
  449:     if "thyroid" in r or r == "mtc" or "c-cell" in r or "c cell" in r:
  450:         return "thyroid C-cell signal"
  451:     if "gallbladder" in r or "cholelithiasis" in r or "cholecystitis" in r:
  452:         return "gallbladder disease"
  453:     # Common single-word endpoints — passthrough lowercase
  454:     if r in (
  455:         "nausea", "vomiting", "diarrhea", "diarrhoea", "constipation",
  456:         "abdominal pain", "hypoglycemia", "hypoglycemic",
  457:         "pancreatitis", "retinopathy", "discontinuation",
  458:         "dyspepsia", "decreased appetite",
  459:     ):
  460:         if r == "diarrhoea":
  461:             return "diarrhea"
  462:         if r == "hypoglycemic":
  463:             return "hypoglycemia"
  464:         return r
  465:     return r
  466: 
  467: 
  468: # Codex Step 3k diff iter-3: raise from 14 to 30. The original 14
  469: # was hit BEFORE the `||` row terminator in 5-arm tables (each arm
  470: # has 2 columns: "n (pct)" + "No. of events"), producing rows that
  471: # spilled across multiple actual rows.
  472: _MAX_PIPES_PER_ROW = 30
  473: # Empty-cell row separator pattern (markdown tables concatenated in
  474: # a single line use "| |" as the row boundary).
  475: _ROW_BOUNDARY_RE = re.compile(r"\|\s*\|")
  476: 
  477: 
  478: def _detect_all_table_regions(direct_quote: str) -> list[tuple[int, int]]:
  479:     """Codex Step 3k diff iter-2 P1 continuing: suppress legacy walk
  480:     inside ANY pipe-rich region, not just safety-header rows. Catches
  481:     descriptive sub-headers like 'Adverse events occurring in ≥5% of
  482:     patients' which are still inside the table block.
  483: 
  484:     Returns list of (start, end) byte ranges in direct_quote where the
  485:     pipe-density is high enough to be a table block. Heuristic: any
  486:     window of 500 chars containing ≥6 `|` is part of a table; expand
  487:     to the surrounding pipe-rich neighborhood.
  488:     """
  489:     if "|" not in direct_quote:
  490:         return []
  491:     pipe_positions = [i for i, c in enumerate(direct_quote) if c == "|"]
  492:     if len(pipe_positions) < 6:
  493:         return []
  494:     regions: list[tuple[int, int]] = []
  495:     # Group consecutive pipes where adjacent pipes are within 200 chars.
  496:     # iter-3: raised from 80 to 200 to span descriptor cells like
  497:     # "Adverse events occurring in ≥0.2% of the overall population
  498:     # (i.e., 3 patients) and leading to discontinuation of tirzepatide
  499:     # or semaglutide" between pipe-clusters of two data sections.
  500:     cluster: list[int] = [pipe_positions[0]]
  501:     for p in pipe_positions[1:]:
  502:         if p - cluster[-1] <= 200:
  503:             cluster.append(p)
  504:         else:
  505:             if len(cluster) >= 6:
  506:                 regions.append((cluster[0], cluster[-1] + 1))
  507:             cluster = [p]
  508:     if len(cluster) >= 6:
  509:         regions.append((cluster[0], cluster[-1] + 1))
  510:     return regions
  511: 
  512: 
  513: def _iter_safety_table_rows(direct_quote: str) -> list[tuple[str, str, str]]:
  514:     """Detect markdown safety-table rows in `direct_quote`.
  515: 
  516:     A row is a candidate if:
  517:       1. First cell (preceded by `|` or line start) matches
  518:          _SAFETY_TABLE_HEADER_RE
  519:       2. Row has >= 3 pipe-separated data cells AFTER the header
  520:       3. Row terminates at: newline, empty-cell row separator (`| |`),
  521:          OR _MAX_PIPES_PER_ROW pipes (whichever comes first)
  522: 
  523:     Returns list of (endpoint_canonical, row_text, raw_endpoint_text).
  524: 
  525:     Header occurrences NOT inside a `|...|` row structure (i.e. in
  526:     prose) are skipped. Each header occurrence is matched at most once.
  527:     """
  528:     rows: list[tuple[str, str, str, int]] = []
  529:     text = direct_quote
  530:     seen_starts: set[int] = set()
  531:     for hdr in _SAFETY_TABLE_HEADER_RE.finditer(text):
  532:         endpoint_text = hdr.group("endpoint")
  533:         # Codex Step 3k diff iter-3 P1: use hdr.start("endpoint") not
  534:         # hdr.start(). The `^\W+` prefix consumes leading symbols, so
  535:         # hdr.start() is at position 0 (before `|`), forcing left_idx
  536:         # to -1. Use the named group's start so left-scan finds the
  537:         # actual `|` before the endpoint name.
  538:         endpoint_start = hdr.start("endpoint")
  539:         # Header must be inside a pipe-delimited structure. Codex Step 3k
  540:         # diff iter-2 P2: walk LEFT until we find `|`, allowing arbitrary
  541:         # cell content (e.g., "| Elevated blood calcitonin level |"
  542:         # where the endpoint vocab "calcitonin" is not at cell start).
  543:         # iter-3: bounded to 80 chars (typical cell width). Larger
  544:         # scans land in unrelated cells.
  545:         left_idx = endpoint_start - 1
  546:         scan_steps = 0
  547:         while left_idx >= 0 and scan_steps < 80:
  548:             if text[left_idx] == "|":
  549:                 break
  550:             if text[left_idx] == "\n":
  551:                 left_idx = -1
  552:                 break
  553:             left_idx -= 1
  554:             scan_steps += 1
  555:         if left_idx < 0 or scan_steps >= 80 or text[left_idx] != "|":
  556:             continue
  557:         # Codex Step 3k diff iter-1 P1 #1: relax the right side — the
  558:         # cell can contain additional text after the matched endpoint
  559:         # phrase. The right boundary is the next `|`, not immediately
  560:         # after the match end.
  561:         right_idx = text.find("|", hdr.end())
  562:         if right_idx < 0:
  563:             continue
  564:         # Avoid pathological gap (header matches but next `|` is too far,
  565:         # e.g., in prose): reject if first-cell length > 200 chars.
  566:         if right_idx - left_idx > 200:
  567:             continue
  568:         # Dedup: avoid matching the same header position twice via
  569:         # overlapping regex matches.
  570:         if left_idx in seen_starts:
  571:             continue
  572:         seen_starts.add(left_idx)
  573:         # Walk forward from right_idx (the `|` right of header) counting
  574:         # data cells. Stop at: newline, empty-cell boundary `| |`, OR
  575:         # _MAX_PIPES_PER_ROW pipes total.
  576:         pipe_count = 1  # the `|` between header and first data cell
  577:         i = right_idx
  578:         row_end = right_idx
  579:         while i < len(text) and pipe_count <= _MAX_PIPES_PER_ROW:
  580:             ch = text[i]
  581:             if ch == "\n":
  582:                 break
  583:             if ch == "|":
  584:                 # Empty-cell row boundary check: is the next non-space
  585:                 # also `|`? If so, this is the row terminator.
  586:                 j = i + 1
  587:                 while j < len(text) and text[j] in " \t":
  588:                     j += 1
  589:                 if j < len(text) and text[j] == "|":
  590:                     # Empty cell ahead — row ends at THIS pipe.
  591:                     row_end = i
  592:                     break
  593:                 pipe_count += 1
  594:                 row_end = i
  595:             i += 1
  596:         # Require >= 3 data cells in the row (3 pipes after the
  597:         # header-right pipe).
  598:         if pipe_count < 4:
  599:             continue
  600:         row_text = text[left_idx:row_end + 1]
  601:         rows.append((endpoint_text.strip().lower(), row_text, endpoint_text, left_idx))
  602:     return rows
  603: 
  604: 
  605: def _extract_cell_percentages(row_text: str, header_end_idx: int) -> list[tuple[float, int, int, str]]:
  606:     """For a table row, extract per-cell percentages.
  607: 
  608:     Returns list of (numeric_value, abs_start, abs_end, raw_text).
  609:     abs_start/end are offsets WITHIN the row_text. Caller adjusts to
  610:     direct_quote offsets.
  611: 
  612:     Skip:
  613:       - Numbers before header_end_idx (the row header itself)
  614:       - Bare numbers without % or ( ... ) context (Codex P2)
  615:     """
  616:     cells: list[tuple[float, int, int, str]] = []
  617:     # Trailing-% form
  618:     for m in _CELL_PCT_TRAILING_RE.finditer(row_text):
  619:         if m.start() < header_end_idx:
  620:             continue
  621:         cells.append((float(m.group("val")), m.start("val"), m.end("val"), m.group(0)))
  622:     # Parenthetical form
  623:     for m in _CELL_PCT_PAREN_RE.finditer(row_text):
  624:         if m.start() < header_end_idx:
  625:             continue
  626:         # Don't double-count if this paren cell already matched %
  627:         already = any(
  628:             c[1] == m.start("val") and c[2] == m.end("val")
  629:             for c in cells
  630:         )
  631:         if not already:
  632:             cells.append((float(m.group("val")), m.start("val"), m.end("val"), m.group(0)))
  633:     return cells
  634:

  193:         EvidencePool when retrieval ran (regardless of adequacy verdict).
  194:             Caller inspects pool.adequacy.is_adequate to decide whether
  195:             to flow to slice 003 generation.
  196:         RetrievalError when the decision is structurally ineligible
  197:             (wrong status, wrong scope_class, or fetch backend fails).
  198:     """
  199:     err = _validate_decision(decision)
  200:     if err is not None:
  201:         return err
  202: 
  203:     started = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
  204:     t_start = time.perf_counter()
  205: 
  206:     queries = plan_queries(decision)
  207: 
  208:     # Run each query, classify each fetch result, keep only allowed-tier sources
  209:     raw_sources: list[Source] = []
  210:     for query in queries:
  211:         try:
  212:             results = fetch_fn(query)
  213:         except NotImplementedError:
  214:             return RetrievalError(
  215:                 code="fetch_backend_unavailable",
  216:                 message=(
  217:                     "fetch_fn is the sentinel default; inject a real "
  218:                     "fetcher (PR 7) or a test stub"
  219:                 ),
  220:                 decision_id=decision.decision_id,

.codex\I-meta-002-q1-launch\codex_readiness_brief.md:23:# Codex readiness gate — I-meta-002 Q1 LIVE-RUN LAUNCH (#938). Pre-spend. APPROVE = the FOUR-ROLE pipeline is ready to start the FIRST paid question (Q1) without a "shit show", given the runbook's blockers are honored.
.codex\I-meta-002-q1-launch\codex_readiness_brief.md:25:The operator's bar for Q1: (a) reasoning and output/verdict content are CLEANLY SEPARATED everywhere — never mixed into one "soap"; (b) FULL per-call run logging so every model call can be reviewed line-by-line ("alphabet level"); (c) all launch blockers surfaced and correctly ordered; (d) NO spend until Codex APPROVE + operator promotes the lock. Rule on whether the runbook (`.codex/I-meta-002-q1-launch/runbook.md`) correctly captures readiness, and whether the verifier-reasoning gap below is a REAL pre-Q1 blocker (P1) or acceptable.
.codex\I-meta-002-q1-launch\codex_readiness_brief.md:29:2. **Verifier transport (Mirror/Sentinel/Judge) reads ONLY `content`.** `src/polaris_graph/roles/openai_compatible_transport.py:305 content = message.get("content")`; `_parse` returns `(raw_text=content, served_model, usage)`. It does NOT read or persist `reasoning_content`. Consequence (a): the verifiers' reasoning is NOT logged anywhere — you cannot line-by-line review WHY Mirror/Sentinel/Judge ruled. Consequence (b): the Judge parser does an EXACT match against the 5-enum after `.strip()` (`judge_contract.py:45,52`) with NO `<think>` stripping; the Mirror parser strips only its own `<co>…</co:doc_id>` tags (`mirror_contract.py:121,141`). So if the served Qwen Judge emits reasoning INLINE as `<think>…</think>` in `content` (rather than a separate `reasoning_content` field), the Judge verdict won't parse → fail-closed (UNREACHABLE / raise), holding every claim. That is safe (no soap reaches the report) but is a functional Q1 risk.
.codex\I-meta-002-q1-launch\codex_readiness_brief.md:33:6. **Budget:** canary cap is `PG_MAX_COST_PER_RUN` (must be set for Q1). Vast $300 / OpenRouter $50 Codex-approved for the 1-question canary. Q1 is a clinical question (drb_75); a `four_role_held` (release HELD by S0 exact-source gate) is the SAFE outcome and is NOT a failure — must NOT be weakened to force a release.

 succeeded in 715ms:
    1: """
    2: Contradiction detector — HONEST-REBUILD Phase 3.
    3: 
    4: Finds pairs of evidence statements that directly contradict each other
    5: on the same (subject, predicate, numeric value) tuple. Surfaces these
    6: to the user before synthesis so the generator cannot silently pick one
    7: side.
    8: 
    9: ADDRESSES PG_LB_SA_02_CONTENT_AUDIT Section E-06: the pre-rebuild
   10: pipeline found two conflicting efficacy numbers for semaglutide weight
   11: loss (STEP 1: 14.9% vs STEP 5: 17.4%), and the final report cited only
   12: one without disclosing the range. A reader could not tell whether the
   13: disagreement was stratification, dosing, duration, or cherry-picking.
   14: 
   15: DESIGN:
   16: This detector is deterministic and rule-based. It does NOT use an LLM
   17: to decide whether two claims contradict because LLM-based contradiction
   18: detection has known failure modes on numerical values (confuses 14 and
   19: 17 as "roughly similar" even when it's a 17% relative difference).
   20: 
   21: Approach:
   22:   1. Extract structured claims: (subject, predicate, numeric_value, unit)
   23:      from each evidence row using regex on the direct_quote.
   24:   2. Group claims by normalized (subject, predicate) pair.
   25:   3. Within each group, flag numeric discrepancies > 10% relative
   26:      difference OR > 2.0 absolute unit difference (configurable).
   27:   4. Return a list of ContradictionRecord objects.
   28: 
   29: The caller (Phase 4 synthesis) inserts a disclosure line for each
   30: contradicted claim: "Sources report X (ref A) and Y (ref B). The
   31: reasons for the difference are [analyst note]."
   32: """
   33: 
   34: from __future__ import annotations
   35: 
   36: import logging
   37: import os
   38: import re
   39: from dataclasses import dataclass, field
   40: from typing import Any, Optional
   41: 
   42: logger = logging.getLogger("polaris_graph.contradiction_detector")
   43: 
   44: 
   45: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   46: # Numeric + unit extraction
   47: # ─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
   48: 
   49: # Percentage values. Captures the number + "%" or " percent".
   50: # Note: \b after "%" fails because % and space are both non-word chars —
   51: # use a non-capturing boundary or a literal end-of-token check instead.
   52: _PCT_RE = re.compile(
   53:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>%|percent|pct)(?=\s|[,.;:)\]!?]|$)",
   54:     re.IGNORECASE,
   55: )
   56: 
   57: # Mass / dose values with unit.
   58: _DOSE_RE = re.compile(
   59:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>mg|µg|ug|mcg|g|kg)(?=\s|[,.;:)\]!?]|$)",
   60:     re.IGNORECASE,
   61: )
   62: 
   63: # HbA1c points. "percentage points" uses an explicit trailing word
   64: # boundary since "points" ends on a word char.
   65: _HBA1C_RE = re.compile(
   66:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>%|percentage\s*points?)",
   67:     re.IGNORECASE,
   68: )
   69: 
   70: # Time durations
   71: _DURATION_RE = re.compile(
   72:     r"(?P<value>-?\d+(?:\.\d+)?)\s*(?P<unit>weeks?|months?|years?)\b",
   73:     re.IGNORECASE,
   74: )
   75: 
   76: 
   77: # Predicate keywords — the ones we most want to catch contradictions on.

src/polaris_graph/generator\multi_section_generator.py:710:11. **Jurisdictional precision (M-29, for multi-authority synthesis)**: When citing regulatory, standards-setting, or governance sources from more than one jurisdiction (different countries, agencies, courts, or rulemaking bodies), attribute every specific assertion to the ONE jurisdiction whose source supports it. Do NOT use generic plural language like "both agencies", "all regulators", "authorities generally", "regulators require", "jurisdictions mandate", or similar when the evidence you cite comes from a single jurisdiction. A boxed warning in one jurisdiction is not the same legal instrument as a precaution in another jurisdiction; a formal contraindication in one framework is not automatically equivalent to a warning in another. If the evidence supports only one jurisdiction's position, write: "Jurisdiction A's framework classifies X as a contraindication [ev_A]. Jurisdiction B's framework addresses X through warnings and precautions [ev_B]." Only collapse to "both" / "all" / "generally" when you have a citation from each referenced jurisdiction in the SAME sentence proving the shared position.

There is downstream markdown safety-table atom logic in `claim_atom_extractor.py:371-633`, but it only helps if pipe-style table text is already present in `direct_quote`; the live fetch path does not preserve/source-extract HTML/PDF result tables structurally.
